170 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Kūfah

Maytham al-Tammār
Maytham, son of Yahyā, was a
slave from the Banī Asad tribe in
the land of Nihrawān.1 Some also
consider him to be Iranian. Amīr
al-Muʾminīn (ʿa) purchased and set
him free. He was given the title alTammār, which means the one who
sells dates, as this was his job.

When Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) asked him for
his name, he replied, “Salīm.”
The Imām (ʿa) then told him, “The
Noble Prophet (ṣ) has told me that
your real name is Maytham (the
name which was given to you by
your parents).
Maytham replied, “The
Noble Prophet (ṣ) and

Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) speak the truth. My
name is Maytham.”
Then, the Imām (ʿa) replied,
“Indeed, your original name is
better for you.”2
Maytham was among the special
companions of Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) and
learned many things based on
his capacity. The Imām (ʿa) also
informed him of many secrets and
hidden realities, as well as future

Maytham al-Tammār 171

Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) told Maytham how he
would be martyred:

“Once I am gone, they will capture
you and hang you. On the third day,
blood will flow from your nose and
mouth and will dye your beard; you
will be among those ten people
who will be hung in front of Amr ibn
Hārith’s house. Your tree will be the
shortest one.” Then, the Imām (ʿa)
actually showed him the palm tree
and said, “You will be hung from
this tree.”

Shrine of Maytham at-Tammār
events to the point that even Ibn
ʿAbbās took lessons from Maytham.
Maytham was imprisoned by Ibn
Ziyād at the same time as Mukhtār
ibn Abī ʿUbayd ath-Thaqafī.
Shaykh al-Mufīd writes, “Maytham
told Mukhtār in prison, 'You will rise
up to seek revenge for Ḥusayn ibn
ʿAlī (ʿa) and will kill this person who
wants to kill you now.' When Ibn
Ziyād was about to kill Mukhtār, he
received a letter from Yazīd to set
Mukhtār free.'”3

One day, Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) called
Maytham and asked him, “O
Maytham! If Ibn Ziyād summons
you and asks you to abandon me,
what will you do?”
Maytham replied, “O Amīr alMuʾminīn (ʿa) I will never abandon
or disassociate from you.”
The Imām (ʿa) said, “They will kill
you and hang you from your date
palm.”
He said, “I will be patient.”
Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) said, “In this case, you
will be with me in the hereafter.”4
Many historians have reported that

1. Nihrawān is a place in ʿIrāq located
between Wāsit and Baghdad; it used to
be part of Irān, and was captured by the
Muslims on their first attack.
2. Ibn Ḥajar Asqalānī, al-Iṣābah, Vol. 6,
P. 249
3. Shaykh al-Mufīd, al-Irshād, Vol. 1,
P. 32
4. Thaqafī Kūfī, al-Ghārāt, P. 572

172 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Kūfah
After the martyrdom of Imām ʿAlī
(ʿa), Maytham used to come by
that palm tree and would pray
and talk with the tree. He would
tell Amr ibn Hārith, “Soon, I will
be your neighbor. Be a good
neighbor for me.”

Maytham replied, “He is on the watch for the oppressors, and you are
one of them.”7
Finally, he was hung, just as Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) had foretold, but even as
they hung him, he wouldn’t stop praising the Ahl al-Bayt (ʿa) or stop
mentioning the evil conduct of Banī Umayyah. Therefore, Ibn Ziyād
ordered his men to cut off his tongue and kill him. He was the first
Muslim to be martyred in such a manner.

Amr didn’t know what he was
talking about and asked him, “Do
you want to buy Ibn Masʿūd’s
house or Ibn Hakim’s?”6
Maytham performed Hajj during
his last year of life, and went to
visit Umm Salamah in Madīnah.
When he asked for news of Imām
Ḥusayn (ʿa), she told him, “I have
heard the Noble Prophet (ṣ)
mention you to Amīr al-Muʾminīn
(ʿa) many times, and Imām
Ḥusayn (ʿa) would mention you a
lot as well.”
When Maytham returned to
Kūfah, Ubaydullāh ibn Ziyād
captured him. This was 10 days
before Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) entered
the land of Karbalāʾ.
He asked Maytham, “Where is
your Allah?”

6. Ibn Ḥajar Asqalānī, al-Iṣābah, Vol.
6, P. 250
7. Ibid

176 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Kūfah

The Home of Imām ʿAlī (ʿa)
When Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) moved to
Kūfah and decided to establish his
government headquarters there,
he needed a place to live. His
followers encouraged him to live in
Dār al-ʿImārah, which was a large,
luxurious castle in which all the
rulers would live. However, Imām
ʿAlī (ʿa) refused. He looked toward
the castle and said that whoever
lived in this place would have a bad
ending. Sure enough, after him, Dār
al-ʿImārah was cursed. Those who
lived there were killed or humiliated.
Instead, the Imām (ʿa) built five rooms for his children, and their families. This is the home
that we see today.
The people objected to this and asked him why he chose to live in such a simple dwelling.
He told them to go search in Kūfah. If they were to find a home that was smaller than his,
then he would be to blame for living in a home larger than the average person. However, if
all the homes in Kūfah were larger than his, then he would build a bigger home.
The size of Imām ʿAlī's home was equivalent to the average home size of the poor
individuals of Kūfah. As Imām, he knew that his duty was to live at the same level as the
lowest class, so that they never felt their Imām was unreachable. From this, we learn an
important lesson. If we want to have a better connection with Allah, the size of our home is
irrelevant, as long as our taqwā is ever-increasing.

The Home of Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) 177

The Imām's home was right next to Masjid al-Kūfah, and
this is where he would establish his prayers everyday
until he was martyred in this very masjid.
The home of the Imām also contains a well, from which
many zāʾirīn seek blessings. Although it was customary
for people to have wells in their homes, this well is
special because the Imām (ʿa) dug it himself. He used
to perform wudūʾ from this well. Moreover, his ghusl almayyit was performed with the water from this well. This
well held a dear place in the Imām's heart. The well now
connects with pipes to the fountains found behind his
house.

178 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Kūfah

Masjid Ṣaʿṣaʿah ibn Ṣawḥān &
Masjid Zayd ibn Ṣawḥān
Ṣawḥān was a famous companion of Imām
ʿAlī (ʿa). A look at the life of Ṣawḥān and his
sons depicts a clear picture of obedience and
devotion to Imām ʿAlī (ʿa).
Ṣawḥān had four sons who were all among
the loyal companions of Amīr al-Muʾminīn (ʿa):
Zayd, Ṣaʿṣaʿah, ʿAbdullah, and Sayḥān.
These two old masājid are located close to

Masjid al-Sahlah and are named after two

Ṣawḥān was a Jew who lived in Khaybar. Upon loyal and sincere companions of Amīr alMuʾminīn (ʿa).
witnessing the Imām (ʿa) lift the gate during
the Battle of Khaybar, his son, Ṣaʿṣaʿah was
amazed and embraced Islām. Ṣawḥān became very upset by this and said, "O my son!
He is only able to lift the gate because he is a magician!" Still, Ṣaʿṣaʿah knew the truth and
become a loyal companion of the Imām (ʿa).
A few years later, Ṣawḥān travelled to Madināh, looking for his son, Ṣaʿṣaʿah, whom he
still loved very much. At this time, the Prophet (ṣ) had died, and there was a struggle for
the khilāfah. At this time, Ṣawḥān saw Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) being dragged through the streets in
chains. When he saw this, he immediately accepted Islām.
Ṣaʿṣaʿah asked, "O Father, what has made you accept Islām now?"
His father replied, "When I saw his miracle at Khaybar, I thought he was a magician. But
now that I have seen him stay silent, despite his great strength and power, in order to
defend the truth, it is clear to me that he is the true leader. All the signs in our book clearly
apply to him."

Zayd ibn Ṣawḥān 179

Ṣaʿṣaʿah ibn Ṣawḥān
According to Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa), "None of Imām ʿAlī's (ʿa)
companions recognized his rights the way Ṣaʿṣaʿah and his
companions did.
Ṣaʿṣaʿah participated in all three battles with Imām ʿAlī (ʿa).
During the Battle of Jamal, after Sayḥān and Zayd were martyred,
Ṣaʿṣaʿah upheld the flag. During the Battle of Ṣiffīn, when
Muʿāwiyah blocked the water for Imām ʿAlī’s (ʿa) army, the Imām
(ʿa) sent Ṣaʿṣaʿah to negotiate with Muʿāwiyah. He was also a
negotiator during the Battle of Nihrawān.

Gravesite of Ṣaʿṣaʿah ibn Ṣawḥān Askar, Bahrain

Additionally, Ṣaʿṣaʿah was one of the only companions who carried the janāzah of Imām ʿAlī (ʿa). After the Imām's
death, Muʿāwiyah tried to have Ṣaʿṣaʿah curse Imām ʿAlī (ʿa), but he refused and instead cursed Muʿāwiyah. Thus,
he was exiled to Bahrain and passed away there in the year 56 AH.
Masjid al-Ṣaʿṣaʿah is a place where he used to perform ʿibādah. From our traditions, we also understand that
Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) prayed here, as well as Imām al-Mahdī (ʿaj), who also recited the special duʿā of Rajab here.
Upon entering this masjid, one should offer two rakaʿāt of Taḥiyyat al-Masjid, recite the special duʿā of this masjid,
and recite the duʿā for the month of Rajab.

Zayd ibn Ṣawḥān
It has been narrated that the Noble Prophet (ṣ) had told Zayd, “A part
of you will go to heaven before you.” Sure enough, during the time of
the third khalīfah, Zayd was exiled to Damascus, and his left hand
was cut off during the conquest of Nahavand, a city in Irān.
He was martyred in the Battle of Jamal.
It has been narrated from Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) that when Zayd fell
on the ground during the battle, Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) went to his side and
cried out:
ُ
ْ
ْ

َ َ َ ْ ُ َ َ َ ََْ َ
َ
َ ََْ
‫اهلل کنت خ ِفيْف المؤن ِه ع ِظيْ َم ال َم ُع ْون ِة‬
‫يازيد! ر مِحك‬‭‬

O Zayd! May Allah have mercy on you! You asked for so little, but
gave so much.
Masjid al-Zayd has now become a part of Masjid al-Sahlah. The
recommended Aʿmāl for this masjid is to offer two-rakaʿāt of Taḥiyyat
al-Masjid and recite the special duʿā for the masjid.

Gravesite of Zayd ibn Ṣawḥān

180 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Kūfah

Dār al-Imārah

Dār al-Imārah, the governor's court, was built by Sa’d ibn Abī Waqqas in the
year 17 AH. It is the oldest Islamic structure in ʿIrāq, after building the Masjid
al-Kūfah. Some of its original pillars and walls still remain today. Muslim
ibn ʿAqīl was martyred in this castle, and the holy heads of Imām Ḥusayn
(ʿa) and the martyrs of Karbalāʾ were displayed here as well. Later, after
Mukhtār’s uprising, the heads of the killers of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) and his
progeny were displayed here. This castle is an excellent example for those
who reflect. As the Qurʾān says:

َ ْ‫أ‬
ُ َ ُ َْ َ
َ ْ ‫الب‬
‫ار‬
‫ص‬
‫ول‬
ِ
ِ‫فاعت رِبوا يا أ ي‬

So take a lesson, O you who have insight! (59:2)
When Moṣʿab ibn Zubayr martyred Mukhtār, ʿAbd al-Malik ibn Marwān came to ʿIrāq and defeated him, and then
entered the Dār al-Imārah. When they presented the head of Moṣʿab to him, a man named Abū Muslim Nakhaʿī
stood and said to ʿAbd al-Malik, “I was in this Dār al-Imārah when the head of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) was presented
Ibn Ziyād, and after some time, the head of Ibn Ziyād was presented to Mukhtār, and later I saw Mukhtār’s head
presented to Moṣʿab and, now I see Moṣʿab’s head presented to you!”
When ʿAbd al-Malik heard of this irony, he became frightened and ordered for Dār al-Imārah to be destroyed.

Masjid as-Sahlah 183

Masjid as-Sahlah
Masjid al-Sahlah is located about 2 kilometers northwest of Masjid al-Kūfah
and was built by Arab tribes during the first century of hijrah. Some say it has
been named after its builder, Saheel. The Masjid was built on the land where
the Abdul Qays tribe lived, and Banī Zafar is a branch of this tribe. Therefore,
it is also sometimes referred to as Masjid as-Saheel, Banī Zafar, and Abdul
Qays.
Ibn al-Faqih narrates that Imām ʿAlī (ʿa) said, “There are four places in Kūfah
where four masaajid have been built.” When asked about those four masaajid,
the Imām (ʿa) replied, “One of them is the Masjid of Zafar or Masjid al-Sahla.”

184 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Masjid as-Sahlah

The Virtues of Masjid as-Sahlah
After Masjid al-Harām, Masjid al-Nabī, and Masjid alKūfah, there is no other masjid as virtuous as Masjid alSahlah. Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) mentions some of its virtues
below:
⁜⁜ It contains the houses of Prophet Idrīs (ʿa), Prophet
Ibrāhīm (ʿa), and Ḥaḍrat Khiḍr (ʿa)
⁜⁜ Imām az-Zamān (ʿaj) will live here with his family
⁜⁜ All 124,000 Prophets have prayed in this masjid
⁜⁜ Residing in this masjid is like residing in the tent of
the Noble Prophet (ṣ)
⁜⁜ Whoever sincerely recites duʿā in this masjid will
receive his/her answer
Then, Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) said, "If I were closer to this
masjid, I would perform all my prayers in it. The virtues
of this masjid are far greater than what I have told you."
Abū Baṣīr replied, “May my life be sacrificed for you!
Will Imām az-Zamān (ʿaj) always reside in this masjid?”
The Imām (ʿa) answered, “Yes. This masjid is among
those places where Allah likes to be worshipped.”
According to Imām as-Ṣadiq (ʿa), there is not a day or
night that passes by where angels are not worshipping
in this masjid.
Additionally, many of the ʿulamāʾʾ have met Imām alMahdī (ʿaj) in this masjid.
1. Biḥār al-Anwār, Vol. 97, P. 436, Ḥadith #6

Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa):

If someone offers a two-rakaʿāt prayer in Masjid
al-Sahlah, Allah will extend his life by two years.1

Prayer of Ḥājāt
It is a tradition of the Prophets and Imāms to offer a tworakaʿāt prayer in Masjid al-Sahlah between Maghrib and
Isha prayers. It has been narrated by Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa)
that if anyone who is grieved performs such a prayer and
then makes duʿā, Allah will remove his pain and sadness.

188 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Masjid as-Sahlah

Maqām Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa)
Bashār Makārī narrates:
One day, I went to visit Imām Jaʿfar aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) in
Kūfah. The Imām (ʿa), who was eating dates, said to me,
“O Bashār! Come closer and enjoy some dates, too.”
I replied, “Please, you enjoy. On my way here, I saw a
scene that hurt my heart and made me lose my appetite.”
However, the Imām (ʿa) insisted that I eat some dates,
so I began eating, too. Then, the Imām asked me, “What
did you see while coming here that made you so upset?”
I said, “I saw that soldiers of the Sulṭān were beating a
woman and dragging her to prison. She was begging for

help, but no one was helping her.”

The Imām asked, “Why were they hitting her?”
I said, “I heard from people that she had said. ‘O
Fāṭimah! May Allah curse those who oppressed you!’”
When the Imām heard this, he stopped eating and
started crying so much that his blessed beard and
handkerchief became soaked. Then, he said to me,
“O Bashār! Let’s go to Masjid al-Sahlah and pray to
Allah for the release of that woman.”
As we headed towards the Masjid, some shīʿah
were also going to Dār al-Khilāfah to see what would
happen to that woman.
When we reached the Masjid, each one of us offered

a two-rakāʿat of prayer in the corner. Afterwards,
Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) raised his hands and recited this
duʿā:

ْ ْ‫خ‬
ْ َ َ ٰ ٓ َ‫َ ْ َ ُ ا‬
ُ
ُ ‫و‬‭
ُ ‫ت‬
.‭..‫م ِعيْ ُده ْم‬‭
‬َ ‫ق‬
‬ ِ ‫الَل‬‭‫مبْ ِد ْي ُ‬ء‬‭
‬ َ ‫أن‬‭‬‫ ِإل‬‭‫ ِإل ‬ه‬‭‬‫ل‬‭‫اهلل‬‭
‬ ‫ت‬
‬ ‫أن‬

You are Allah; there is no god except You. You
initiated creation and will resurrect them...

Maqām Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) 189

was free and could go home, so the woman returned to
her home."
Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) asked, “The woman refused to take
the 20 dirham from him?”
The man replied, “Yes, by Allah, even though she was in
need of that money.”

The Imām (ʿa) handed me seven dirhams from his pocket
Then, the Imām went into sujūd and recited a dhikr
and said, “Go to her home and convey my salām to her,
that I could not hear. Then, he lifted his head and said,
and give her this money, too.”
“Get up! The woman has just been released.”
We came out of the Masjid and came across someone
who was returning from Dār al Khilāfah.
The Imām asked him, “What is the news of the
woman?”
The man replied, “She was released!”
The Imām asked, “Why did they release her?”

So, we went to her home and conveyed the Imām’s
salām to her. The woman replied, “I ask you by Allah, did
the Imām (ʿa) really send his salām upon me?”
I replied, “I swear by Allah, Imām as-Ṣadiq (ʿa) sent his
salām to you.”
At this time, she gasped and fainted. We waited for her to
regain consciousness. She then said, “What did you say?
Can you repeat it?”

He replied, “I didn't understand, but I was standing at
the door of Dār al-Khilāfah when a guard came out
and asked the woman, 'What did you say?'

We repeated the message three times and then gave her
the money and told her that the Imām (ʿa) sent it for her.

The woman replied, 'I said, ‘O Fāṭimah! May Allah
curse those who oppressed you!''

The woman took the money and said, “Please ask the
Imām to ask Allah to forgive my sins. There is no better
intercessor than him and his grandfathers!”

The Sulṭān ordered the guard to give her 200 dirhams
and ask him for forgiveness.
The woman refused to take the money. When the
guard saw this, he went back to Dār al-Khilāfah. After
some time, he came out and told the woman that she

When I returned to Imām as-Ṣadiq (ʿa) and told him what
happened, the Imām made duʿā for her while crying.
Muḥammad bin Jaʿfar Mashhadī, Al Mazār al-Kabīr, P. 136-140

190 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Masjid as-Sahlah
Sayyid bin Ṭāwūs said: Go to Masjid al-Sahlah on Tuesday night because
it is better than any other times. After reciting Maghrib prayers and its
nawāfil, go to the middle of the Masjid (Maqām Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa)) and
offer a two rakaʿāt prayer with the intention of Taḥiyyat al-Masjid. Then,
recite another two rakaʿāt prayer with the intention of Maqām Imām aṣṢādiq (ʿa). Then, raise your hand and recite the following duʿā:

Notes/Reflections

َ‫َ ْ َ ا‬
‫كربـلء‬

Karbalāʾ

204 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Karbalāʾ
Dear Zāʾir,
Welcome to Heaven on Earth. Welcome to the sanctuary over which the angels yearn for the opportunity to visit
as well a land that witnessed the salvation of Islam. Welcome to the land whose tragedy will be avenged only
with the advent of the Awaited Savior. As you tread these lands, let one of your main duʿās be for the return of
the Imām (ʿaj) and to be included amongst his companions, just like the 72.
Although many stores and hotels have been constructed in this area, and it may be different to one's imagination,
remember that you are still walking in the same lands that Imām Ḥusayn (A) roamed.
In this city, you will find the following landmarks:
•
The holy shrine of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
•
The holy shrine of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās
•
Mukhayyam (Campsite)
•
Tall az-Zaynabīyyah (Hill of Zaynab)
•
Sites of martyrdom
•
Other holy landmarks
Inside the ḥaram of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa), you will find:
• The six-cornered ḍarīḥ, which contains:
• The grave of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
• The grave of Ḥaḍrat ʿAlī Akbar
• The grave of Ḥaḍrat ʿAlī Asghar
• The ḍarīḥ of the companions
• The ḍarīḥ of Ḥabīb ibn Muẓāhir
• The ḍarīḥ of Ibrāhīm al-Mujāb
• The Madhbah (Site of martyrdom)

Karbalāʾ 205

Karbalāʾ
Karbalāʾ is located on the western side of the Euphrates River, about 67 miles (108 km) from Baghdad.
Its history dates back to Babylonian times. Some historians assert that the word “Karbalāʾ” has been
derived from the ancient Babylonian language and means “closeness to God”(‫)قرب الل‬.
Other people date its history back to ancient civilizations, due to the various remains and ancient
temples in the city. The word Karbalāʾ is a compound word of two Assyrian words: "karb" — meaning
shrine — and "ala" — meaning God; hence, the combination results in “Shrine of God.”
More famously, Karbalāʾ comes from the two words "Karb" (hardships) and "Balāʾ" (difficulties)
beacuse when Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) reached this land, he asked what it was called. Upon hearing the
name "Karbalāʾ," he said the following:

َ‫ْ ا‬
َ ْ
َ ُ َ ْ ِّ‫َ َّ ُ َّ ي‬
‫ن أ ُع ْوذ بِك ِم َن الك ْر ِب َو البَلء‬
‫اللهم ِإ‬

O Allah! Certainly, I seek refuge with You from the hardships and difficulties.
Other names for Karbalāʾ are "Ṭaf" and Ḥira" (known as “Ḥāʾir” today), which means “the land which
refused to allow water into it.” It was given this name because when the ʿAbbāsid khalīfah Mutawakkil
ordered the holy shrine to be destroyed and flooded, the water miraculously stopped when it reached
the holy grave, and instead went around it. This land was just a barren desert until the year 61 AH.
However, after the tragedy of Karbalāʾ and construction of the holy shrines, it has become the center
of pilgrimage in Iraq.

206 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) and his caravan arrived
in Karbalāʾ on the 2nd of Muḥarram, 61 AH.
According to some narrations, Imām Ḥusayn
(ʿa) bought a piece of land, about 36 km2 in
size (about 14 mi2), for 6,000 dirhams from
the people of Naynavā and Ghāziriyah. In the
contract, he placed a condition that the sellers
must guide the pilgrims in performing ziyārah
of his grave and host them for three days.
Today, that land is where Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
and his companions are buried.
Majmaʿ al-Baḥrayn,Vol.4P.32, Ṭarīḥī

Karbalāʾ 207
Today, the city of Karbalāʾ is about 43 km2 (about 16 mi2), and the barren desert that was
once filled with sand and rocks has been replaced with buildings and gardens that are watered by the Euphrates River. There are two main roads leading into the city: one from Najaf
and another from Baghdad, which is 97 km long (about 60 miles) and goes through the city
of Musayyab.
Karbalāʾ can be divided into two parts: the older Karbalāʾ and the new Karbalāʾ (based on
construction). The new Karbalāʾ contains tall buildings, wide roads, and most of the government buildings, religious schools, and other infrastructure.
The most well-known neighborhoods are Bāb as-Salālimah, Bāb at-Ṭāq, Bāb al-Baghdad,
Bāb al-Khān, Mukhayyim, Bāb an-Najaf, and Eastern and Western ʿAbbāsiyah.
New quarters have also been added, such as the quarters of al-Ḥusayn (ʿa), Muʿalimān, alʿAbbās (ʿa), an-Naqīb, Ḥurr, and Ramaḍān.

The Ṣalāh (Prayer) of
Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
Each Maʿṣūm has a special ṣalāh that can
be found in Mafātiḥ al-Jinān.
The prayer of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) consists of
four rakaʿāt with two salāms (like two sets
of Fajr prayers). In each rakʿah:
• Recite Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and Sūrah alIkhlāṣ 50 times each in qiyām (standing).
• Then, go into rukūʿ and recite each
sūrah 10 times.
• Then, stand from rukūʿ, and recite each
sūrah 10 times.
• Then, perform sajdah and recite each
sūrah 10 times.
• Then, sit up in julūs, and recite each
sūrah 10 times.
• Then, perform sajdah again, and recite
each sūrah 10 times.
• Repeat this method in all four rakaʿāt.
After completing the prayer, recite the accompanying duʿā, which can be found in
Mafātiḥ al-Jinān.

History of the Shrine
 61 AH: The Banī Asad tribe buried the holy bodies of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa), Ḥaḍrat
ʿAbbās (ʿa), and the other martyrs and built a holy grave over them, under the
guidance of Imām as-Sajjād (ʿa).


65 AH: Mukhtār ath-Thaqafī built a dome over the holy grave using bricks and
plaster, and placed two gates around it.

 132 AH: Abū al-ʿAbbās Safāḥ expanded the haram by creating an adjacent annex
next to the Imām’s (ʿa) holy grave.
 146 AH: Abū Jaʿfar Manṣūr destroyed the annex.
 158 AH: Mahdī ʿAbbāsī rebuilt the annex.
 171 AH: Harūn ʿAbbāsī destroyed the entire shrine and cut down the cedar tree
next to it.
 193 AH: ʾAmīn ʿAbbāsī rebuilt the shrine.
 236 AH: Mutawakkil ʿAbbāsī destroyed the shrine of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) and
plowed its land.
 247 AH: Muntaṣir ʿAbbāsī rebuilt the ḥaram. Sayyid Ibrāhīm al-Mujāb and his
tribe became the first to reside near the holy shrine, and his tribe, the ʿAlavian,
followed in his footsteps.
 273 AH: Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad ibn Zayd, the leader of the Tabarestan
movement, gradually rebuilt the haram.
 280 AH: Dāʿī ʿAlavī built a dome over the holy grave.
 367 AH: ʿAḍud ad-Dawlah daylamī built a dome with four porches and a ḍarīḥ
made of tusk, as well as towers and other construction in the city.
 407 AH: After the candles fell, the shrine was set on fire, but the minister of the
time, Ḥasan ibn al Faḍl, rebuilt the shrine.
 412 AH: Ḥasan ibn al-Faḍl, the state minister of the time, built a second wall
around the city with four metal gates.
 479 AH: Mālik Shāh Saljūqī rebuilt the wall around the shrine.

History of the Shrine 211

 620 AH: Al-Nāṣir li-Dīnillāh ʿAbbāsī built a ḍarīḥ for the shrine.
 767 AH: Sulṭān ʾUways Jalāʾirī built the internal dome and a
porch.
 786 AH: Sulṭān ʾAḥmad ibn ʾUways built two golden minarets
and extended the shrine’s courtyard.

212 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ
� 914 AH: Shāh Ismāʿīl Ṣafawī gilded the shrine and gifted 12 golden lamps to the haram.
� 920 AH: Shāh Ismāʿīl Ṣafawī constructed a box out of teakwood for the ḍarīḥ.
� 932 AH: Shāh Ismāʿīl II gifted a beautiful silver ḍarīḥ to the ḥaram.
� 941 AH: Shāh ʿAbbās Ṣafawī performed a pilgrimage to Karbalāʾ. During this time, he dredged the river and rebuilt the
shrine of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa).
� 953 AH: Shāh Suleymān Qānūnī made further repairs to the shrine and transformed the sandy lands around the area
into gardens.
� 983 AH: ʿAlī Pāshā renovated the dome.
� 1032 AH: Shāh ʿAbbās Ṣafawī built a copper ḍarīḥ and tiled the dome.
� 1048 AH: Sulṭān Murād IV ordered for the dome to be plastered from the outside.
� 1135 AH: Nādir Shāh’s wife donated significant funds for the renovation and extension of the holy shrine.
� 1155 AH: Nādir Shāh ʾAfshār adorned the existing buildings and donated expensive gifts to the shrine.
� 1211 AH: Āghā Muḥammad Khān Qājār ordered the dome to be covered in gold.
� 1216 AH: Wahhabis attacked Karbalāʾ, destroying the ḍarīḥ and the courtyard, and stole its properties. After the
attack, an Indian ruler built beautiful homes and bazaars (shops) in Karbalāʾ. He also built a stronger wall around the
city.
� 1217 AH: Sayyid ʿAlī Tabātabāʿi, author of Al-Riyāḍ, built a fourth wall around the city with six gates.
� 1227 AH: Fatḥʿalī Shāh Qājār ordered for the haram to be renovated the golden plates atop the dome.
� 1232 AH: Fatḥʿalī Shāh Qājār built a silver ḍarīḥ and gilded the courtyard.
� 1250 AH: Fatḥʿalī Shāh Qājār renovated the dome and the courtyard and constructed the dome of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās’s
(ʿa) shrine as well.
� 1273 AH: Nāṣir ad-Dīn Shāh renovated the dome of the shrine of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) and part of its gildings.
� 1285 AH: Midḥat Pāshā set up government buildings and expanded the city.

History of the Shrine 213
� 1418 AH: Due to the Intifāḍah, many people took refuge in the
shrine, but the tyrant Saddam Hussein fired a cannon at the
holy dome, destroying a part of its gilding. He then opened fire
on people, causing mass bloodshed. The bullet holes are still
visible inside the holy shrine.
� 1426 AH: The recent construction consists of building a
second floor for the outer wall of Imam Hussain's Holy Shrine.
It contains a museum, a center for studies, geometrical
sections, halls for conferences and scientific symposiums.
This project will complete roofing the courtyard to increase five
times its capacity. This plan marks a new stage in the history
of Imam Hussain's Holy Shrine. Affiliated to the shrine, Three
pilgrimage cities on the road to Karbala were also built. They
provide free services for pilgrims.
� 1428 AH: In order to enhance the usage of the courtyard and
protect the pilgrims from harsh weather, a roof was built over
the courtyard.
� 1431 AH: The minarets of the shrine of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa)
were gilded.

214 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Intifāḍah al-Shaʿbāniyah
The Intifāḍah al-Shaʿbāniyyah, which took place in
1991, was a very significant event for the Iraqi poeple.
From 1979 to 2003, Iraq was ruled by the evil tyrant
Saddam Hussein, who brutally tortured many Muslims,
especially the Shīʿah. In the year 1991, Saddam attacked Kuwait, but was defeated.
Several days after the army was defeated in Kuwait
and left in a vulnerable state, the Iraqi people decided
to revolt against his oppressive regime. The Shīʿah
were quickly able to gain control over many cities, such
as Kirkuk, and the Baʿth regime was very close to being
overthrown.

After getting the green light to destroy the Shīʿah uprising
from US politicians, the helicopters of Saddam’s army
used tanks to suppress the revolts. Even from within
the Shīʿah, some turned against them and joined the
Ba’athists.

During the Intifāḍah, tens of thousands of Shīʿah within
the deserts, cities, and prisons were martyred. This
event is marked as a “Day of Resistance” in Iraq and
served as a catalyst in overthrowing the oppressive regime of Saddam Hussein.

¾¾Al-Qiblah Gate of the shrine of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa)

After destroying the shrine and killing Shīʿah, the army of
Saddam Hussein take photos of their destruction.

Yaḥyā ibn al-Mughīrah ar-Rāzī has
narrated:
I was near Jarīr ibn ʿAbd al-Ḥamīd,
when a person from Iraq entered.
Jarīr asked, “What is the latest news
in Iraq?”
It was replied, “Hārūn ar-Rashīd
has ordered for the cedar tree of
Karbalāʾ to be cut down.”
Jarīr replied, “Allahu Akbar! There
is a narration from the Prophet (ṣ) where he said three
times, ‘May the curse of Allah be upon the one who cuts
down the cedar tree!’ Now we understand the meaning
of this ḥadīth.”1
The cedar tree marked the grave of Abā ʿAbd Allah and
was located near Bāb as-Sidrah. Hārūn ar-Rashīd cut
down the tree because he did not want anyone to visit
the grave of Abā ʿAbd Allah.
Al-Amālī, P. 325, Shaykh at-Ṭūsī

222 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Hāʾir al-Ḥusaynī: A Place Where Duʿās Are Accepted
In the year 236 AH, Al-Mutawakkil ordered his men to destroy and raze the shrine of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
to the ground. As a result, the area of the Imām’s (ʿa) grave was sunken, almost as if it had become a pit.
He then commanded them to the land with water for farming purposes, but to his surprise, the water would
not enter into the blessed grave of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa); instead, it would flow backwards or around the grave,
almost as if there was an invisible barrier around the grave.
Then, he ordered them to release cows to plow through the land, but even those cows would not walk
over the grave.1 Some have said that because this miraculous occurrence, this land is called “Ḥā’ir”, which
َ which means a pit that is usually filled with water.2
ََ‫”ح ر‬,
comes from the Arabic word “‫ي‬
In present day, the Ḥā’ir is considered that area which is directly beneath the dome and around the ḍarīḥ.
Please note that the gravesite of the 72 martyrs is not included.
1. Biḥār al-Anwār Vol. 98, P. 117
2. Ṣaḥāḥ al-Lughah wa Miṣbāḥ al-Munīr

Abū Hāshim Jaʿfarī narrates:
Once, while Imām al-Hādī (ʿa) was sick, he said, "Send a person towards Hā’ir (to seek a cure for
me)."
I replied, "May my life be sacrificed for you! Will you allow me to go?"
The Imām (ʿa) said, "Yes, go ahead, but go with taqīyyah (concealing your faith)."
I intended to go, but before leaving, I spoke about my trip with ʿAlī ibn Balāl. He was puzzled and
asked, "Imām al-Hādī (ʿa) himself is a Hāʾir (a place/person where duʿā is accepted). What does he
want to do with another Hāʾir?"
I went to the Imām (ʿa) and mentioned ʿAlī ibn Balāl’s question. The Imām (ʿa) replied, "Didn’t the
Noble Prophet (ṣ) perform tawāf around Allah’s House (the Kaʿbah)?
And didn’t he kiss the Ḥajar al-Aswad, despite his status as the Prophet, and despite the status of a
muʾmin (believer) being higher than the House of God?!
Know that places like Karbalāʾ are those places where Allah loves to be mentioned and called upon.
Likewise, I prefer for people to seek my shifāʾ and cure in places where Allah prefers, and the Hāʾir
Ḥusaynī is one of them."
Kāmil az-Ziyārah, Ch. 90, Ḥadīth #1

Marjaʿs fatwā on ṣalāh in the Shrine of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) 223

Can a Zāʾir Offer Full ṣalāh in the Shrine of
Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)?
Karbalāʾ (Ḥāʾir al-Ḥusaynī) is one of the four places where a
traveller may choose to offer his/her ṣalāh in full or qasr.
In Karbalāʾ, the only area where you may perform your prayers
in full is in the vicinity of the Ḥāʾir. If you are unsure of its vicinity,
then practice iḥtiyāṭ (caution) by praying qasr.
Pilgrims can act according to their Marjaʿs fatwā below:
Āyatullāhs Sistani and Subhani: It is permissible to perform your
prayers within 36 feet of the holy grave; out of precaution, it is better to prayer qasr further out from the ḍarīḥ.
Āyatullāhs Khomeini, Fazel Lankarani, and Khamenei: It is
permissible to perform your prayers in full within 37.7 feet of the
holy grave.
Āyatullāh Vahid Khorasani: It is permissible to perform your
prayers in full within the entire haram.

Āyatullāhs Khoei, Bahjat, Makarim, and Tabrizi: It is permissible to perform your prayers in full around the holy ḍarīḥ (Hā’ir) and
iḥtiyāṭ wājib to perform qasr prayers further out from the ḍarīḥ.
Āyatullāh Safi Golpaygani: It is permissible to perform your
prayers in full within the entire haram.

Āyatullāh Araki and Shubayri Zanjani: A traveller must offer qasr
prayer even in the Ḥāʾir.
Tawḍīʿ al-Masāʾil Marājiʿ, Vol.1, P.753, Rule 1356

224 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) and the
Pigeons
Dawūd ibn Farqad narrates:
I was sitting in the house of Imām aṣṢādiq (ʿa) and noticed a pigeon that
was busy reciting something.
The Imām looked at me and asked, “O
Dawūd, do you know what this bird is
saying?”
I replied, “May I be sacrificed for you. I
don’t know.”
The Imām replied, “He is asking Allah
to withhold His mercy from the killers of
Ḥusayn ibn ʿAlī (ʿa). It is good to keep
these birds in your homes [as pets].”
Kāmil al-Ziyārah, Ibn Qulawayh

He who knows not your love, O Husayn,
has verily lived in vain

Ziyārah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
As you leave your home, keep reciting the following dhikr with humility:
There is no god except Allah! Allah is the
Greatest! All praise is for Allah!

When you enter Karbalāʾ:
 Enter humbly, with a broken heart.
 A pilgrim of Karbalāʾ is like a pilgrim of Makkah; hence, maintain honor, dignity, and
patience, and be a good travel partner for others.
 Protect your gaze, tongue, and hands from forbidden acts. Avoid arguing and holding
grudges against one another. If you maintain such etiquettes, then the rewards of Ḥajj
and ʿUmrah will be written for you, inshā’Allah.
 When you reach the Euphrates, recite the following 100 times each:
¾¾ Allahu Akbar
¾¾ Lā ilāha illAllah
¾¾ Ṣalawāt
 Wear clean clothes and perform ghusl. Then, recite the following duʿā:

‫هلل‬

As you head towards the holy shrine:

Ziyārah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) 227

 Talk less and remember Allah abundantly.
 Start by praising Allah and reciting ṣalawāt as you walk slowly, with complete tranquility.
 Walk modestly and with humility, just as servants and companions would.
 Offer many prayers and recite abundant ṣalawāts
 Before entering the shrine, recite the Idhn ad-Dukhūl (Permission to Enter)
Inside the ḥaram:
 When you enter the ḥaram, head towards Ḥāʾir al-Ḥusaynī and ask for your duʿās,
because this is the place of istijābah (acceptance of duʿās).
 Try to offer your obligatory prayers, as well as recommended prayers, by the Imām’s
(ʿa) grave since it is accepted there. The rewards for performing a wājib (mandatory)
prayer there is equal to performing Ḥajj, and a nāfilah prayer (recommended) is equal to
performing ʿUmrah.
 Ibn Qulawayh narrates from Imām al-Bāqir (ʿa), “Whenever you have a ḥājah (request),
go to the holy grave of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) and offer a four rakaʿāt prayer (in two sets of
two rakaʿāt), and then ask for your request.”
 Among the recommended deeds is reciting ṣalawāt upon him and his holy family.
 Stand behind the head and recite ṣalawāt upon the Noble Prophet (ṣ) and his beloved
family and Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa).
 Recite the tasbīḥ of Amīr al-Muʾminīn 1,000 times by the holy head (If you’re facing
qiblah, the head is located in the furthest part of the ḍarīḥ on your right).
 Recite the tasbīḥ of Sayyidah Faṭimah (ʿa) 1,000 times by the Imām’s (ʿa) foot.
 It is recommended to offer a two rakaʿāt prayer by the holy head in which you recite
Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and Sūrah ar-Raḥmān in the first rakʿah and Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and
Sūrah al-Mulk in the second rakʿah. The reward of this prayer is equal to 25 accepted
Ḥajj alongside the Prophet (ṣ).
It is narrated from Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) that whoever walks to perform the ziyārah
of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa), for each step, Allah will give him/her the reward of 1,000
good actions, forgive 1,000 sins, and elevate his/her status by 1,000 levels.

Ziyārah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) 239
Then, offer a two rakaʿāt prayer by the holy head, just like Fajr. There is also a
recommended two rakaʿāt prayer that is performed in the following method: in the first
rakʿah, recite Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and Sūrah ar-Raḥmān, and in the second, recite Sūrah
al-Fātiḥah and Sūrah al-Mulk. The reward of this prayer is equal to 25 accepted Ḥajj
alongside the Prophet (ṣ). Then, recite the following:

Ziyārat ʿĀshūrāʾ

243

Ziyārat ʿĀshūrāʾ
Sāliḥ ibn ʿUqbah and Sayf ibn ʿUmayrah have reported that ʿAlqamah ibn Muḥammad al-Ḥaḍramī
once asked Imām al-Bāqir (ʿa) to teach him a prayer he could recite when he would visit Imām
Ḥusayn’s (ʿa) shrine on the day of ʿĀshūrāʾ.
He also asked the Imām (ʿa) to teach him another prayer that he could recite from his own home
when he would be unable to visit the shrine on ʿĀshūrāʾ, after which he would point to the shrine
and send greetings to Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa).
The Imām (ʿa) said, “O ʿAlqamah! After you salute Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) with greetings and offer the
two-unit prayer, you may say "Allahu Akbar" and then recite the following ziyārah. If you do so,
you will have recited the prayer that is recited by the angels who visit Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa).
You will also be raised ranks to be included with those who were martyred with him. Moreover,
you will be granted the reward of visiting all the Prophets.”

‫السل ُم‬

254 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Ḥabīb ibn Maḍāhir
Ḥabīb ibn Maḍāhir Asadī was a Kūfi from the Banī Asad tribe, as
well as a revered companion of the Noble Prophet (ṣ). In addition to
participating in all three battles of Jamal, Ṣiffīn, and Nihrawān, he was
also a sincere student of Amīr al-Muʾminīn (ʿa) to the extent that the
Imām (ʿa) had taught him the knowledge of “Manāyā & Balāyā,” which
is knowledge of the inner self.1
Ḥabīb was part of a special unit of the Imām’s (ʿa) army, called
“Shurṭat al-Khamīs.” Ḥabīb was amongst the Shīʿah leaders of Kūfah
who sent letters to Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa). When Muslim ibn ʾAqīl came to
Kūfah, Ḥabīb offered his allegiance and also tried to collect allegiance
from others. Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) wrote him a letter after the martyrdom
of Muslim ibn ʿAqīl, asking him to join him in Karbalāʾ.
Ḥabīb had a high status in the eyes of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa), and when he joined Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) in Karbalāʾ,
he was placed as the commander of the army’s left wing. He also attempted to recruit some men from the Banī
Asad to join the Imām’s (ʿa) army, but the Yazīdi army prevented that from happening.2
Ḥabīb was 75 years at the time of his martyrdom, and his head was placed on a spear, along with others, and
paraded through Kūfah. His grave is apart from the 72 companions because similar to Ḥurr, his tribe came and
buried his body.
Al-Ḥusayn (ʿa) fī Ṭarīqah Ilā ash-Shahādah, P.6
Anṣār al-Ḥusayn, P.66

Allah,

Sayyid Ibrāhīm al-Mujāb
Sayyid Ibrāhīm al Mujāb was the son of Sayyid Muḥammad ʿĀbid, who was one of the
son of Imām Mūsā al-Kāḍim (ʿa). He came to Karbalāʾ in the year 247 AH and settled
there. During that time, Muḥammad Muntaṣir, the son of Mutawakkil, was the ʿAbbāsid
caliph in power. He was very offended by how his father used to treat the Shīʿah and
therefore took a different approach by allowing them to perform ziyārah to the shrine
of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa).
During this time, Sayyid Ibrāhīm came to Karbalāʾ for Ziyārah. When he reached the
Imām’s (ʿa) holy shrine, he faced the holy grave and greeted him:
َ‫َ َ َّ َ َّ ا‬
َ َ
‫لسل ُم َعليْك‬
‫يا جدا ا‬‭‬
Peace be upon you, O Grandfather!
A reply was heard coming out of the grave:
َ‫َ َ دَ َ َ َ ْ َ َّ ا‬
‫السل ُم‬
‫يا ولِي و عليك‬‭‬
And peace be upon you, O Grandson!

Since then, he has been known as Sayyid Ibrāhīm al Mujāb (the one who was answered).

Madhbaḥ: The Place of Martyrdom 257

Madhbaḥ: The Place of Martyrdom

And whoever is killed unjustly,
We have given his heir authority.
(17:33)
This is the place where the head of Imām
Ḥusayn (ʿa) was severed from his body.
This area is covered by a ḍarīḥ to mark
its significance. For men, there is a silver
door leading to this room, and the sister’s
entrance is through the courtyard. This room
is southwest of Ḥabīb ibn Maḍāhir’s grave.

Turbah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
Prophet Muḥammad (ṣ):

َ َ ْ‫أ‬
ُ ِْ‫َ اَ َ َّ إْ َ َ َ حَْ َ ُ َّ َ ِّ َ َ ي‬

َ‫َ َ ْ َ َّ ا‬
ِ ‫علي ِهم السلم ِمن و‬
ِ‫له‬

Know that the answer [to prayers] lies
under his holy dome, and the cure [for
illnesses] lies in his soil and the Imāms (ʿa)
of his lineage.
Mustadrak al-Wasāil, Vol. 10, P. 335

َ‫َ َّ لُ َّ ُ ن‬

Do not take any dirt from my grave as
tabarruk (blessing), for certainly, all dirt is
ḥarām (to eat) except for the dirt (turbah)
of my grandfather, Ḥusayn ibn ʿAlī (ʿa), in
which the Almighty has placed (cure) for
our Shīʿah and intimate servants.
Jāmiʿ Ahādith as-Shīʿah, Vol. 12, P. 533

Turbah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) 261
Aḥkām and Effects of Soil from Imām Ḥusayn’s (ʿa) Grave
 It is mustaḥab (recommended) to prostrate on the turbah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) during
ṣalāh and leads to greater rewards (than without sajdah).1
 Eating any sort of turbah (soil) is ḥarām (forbidden), except for the turbah of Imām Ḥusayn
(ʿa), which you are allowed to have a little of with the intention of attaining cure (shifāʾ).2
 Giving a taste of turbah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) to newborns is mustaḥab.3
 It is necessary to respect the turbah; any sort of disrespectful act towards it is ḥarām,
such as:
¾¾ Making it najis (ritually impure)
¾¾ Throwing it where it is disrespectful (if it falls somewhere disrespectful, it must
be removed)
 It is mustaḥab to place some turbah with a mayyit (dead body) and also mix some into
his/her hunūt4 as well.
 It can be concluded that one’s entire life should be accompanied by the turbah of Imām
Ḥusayn (ʿa).

Al-ʿUrwah al-Wuthqā Vol.1, Fi Masjid al-Jibha, P.646
Tawḍīʿ al Masāʾil, Rule 2628
Taḥrīr al Wasīlah Vol.2, P.310, Rule #2
4
Hunut is a small amount of camphor that is placed on the
following seven parts of sajdah after ghusl al-mayyit: the
forehead, palms of both hands, both knees, and the tips of
both big toes.
1
2
3

262 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Tasbīḥ of Turbah
History of the Tasbiḥ of Turbah
After the Noble Prophet (ṣ) gifted and taught the famous tasbīḥ
of Fāṭimah az-Zahrāʾ (ʿa) to his daughter, she made her own
tasbīḥ using a wool thread with ties.
After the martyrdom of Ḥamzah in the battle of Uḥud, she
replaced the knots in her tasbīḥ with dirt from his grave and used
that for her dhikr. Many followed her lead and did the same.
When Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) was martyred in Karbalāʾ, due to his
unique status and high virtue, his turbah replaced all prior ones.

Madīnah: the pure soil of Sayyid ash-Shuhadāʾ
Ḥamzah ibn ʿAbd al MuṭṭʿAlīb (uncle of the
Prophet) and the martyrs of the battle of Uḥud

Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa): Our Shīʿah are not without need of
five things: a toothbrush, comb, prayer rug, turbah tasbīḥ, and
ʿaqīq (agate) ring1.
Imām ʿAlī ar-Riḍā (ʿa): Whoever recites the following dhikr with
a tasbiḥ made of turbah, with every bead of the tasbīḥ, the Al- Karbalāʾ: the pure soil of Abā ʿAbd Allah al-Ḥusayn
mighty will record for him/her 6,000 good acts, erase 6,000 sins, Reciting dhikr using a tasbīḥ made
elevate him/her 6,000 levels, and write for him/her 6,000 cures2: out of the turbah of Imām Ḥusayn
ْ َ ُ َ ُ َّ‫َ لحَْ ْ ُ َ اَ ٰ َ ا‬
(ʿa) and even just carrying it has
َ َ ْ ُ
‫اهلل أكب‬
‫هلل وا مدلهلِ ِ ول ِإله ِإل اهلل و‬
ِ ‫سبحان ا‬
great rewards.

Turbah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) 263

Imām Ḥusayn’s (ʿa) Turbah
Even though we have many aḥādīth that say where the turbah should be taken from, the
closer the soil is to the grave of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa), the better it is.
ْ َ‫ْ ُ ْ َ لَى‬
َّ ‫طينْ ُ قَبرْ الحْ ُسَينْ َعلَيْه‬
ٌ ‫الس اَلم ِفيْ ِه َش َف‬
ٰ ‫اء َو إِن أخذ‬
‫ع َرأ ِس ِميْل‬
ِ
ِ
ِ
ِ
Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) said: There is cure in Imām Ḥusayn’s (ʿa) turbah
even if it is within 1,800 meters [from his grave].

Wasāʾil as-Shīʿah, Vol. 14, P. 513, H.19718

Some pilgrims came to Iraq and said to Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa), “We know that the turbah of
Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) cures every ailment, but does it also protect and give safety from fear?”
The Imām (ʿa) replied, “Yes, anytime someone wants to find peace and security from what
they fear, they should hold onto the turbah and recite the following duʿā three times:

Turbah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) 265
Then, kiss the turbah, rub it over your eyes, and say:
O Allah, I ask You by the right of this blessed
dust,
by the right of its owner,
by the right of his grandfather,
by the right of his father,
by the right of his mother,
by the right of his brother,
and by the right of his purified sons,
to make it a cure for every ailment,
security against every fear,
and safeguard against every evil.

266 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Kaʿbah & Zamzam; Karbalāʾ & Euphrates
Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa): Indeed Allah, the Blessed and Exalted, has elevated some lands and bodies of water above
others. Some of them boasted to others and some transgressed, and they were punished for not being humble
to Allah. Because of its transgressions, polytheists took over (the land of) Kaʿbah and changed the taste of the
zamzam water. Indeed, the land of Karbalāʾ and Euphrates River were the first land and body of water that
glorified Allah, the Blessed and Exalted.
So, Allah blessed them and said to the Land of Karbalāʾ, “Speak of that with which the Almighty Allah has honored
you, for indeed the lands and the waters have boasted to one another.”
The Land of Karbalāʾ said:

ً ْ ُ ْ َ ْ ْ ُ ْ َ َ‫ِّ َ ُ ْ ُ ْ َ ْ َ َ ْ َ اَ َ ْ َ َ ْ َ َ ٌ َ ْ َ ٌ َ ْ َ َ َ ْ َ اَ َ ْ َ لَى‬
َ َ َ ُ ْ َ َّ َ ُ ْ
ُ ْ َ ََ
ٰ ‫اضعة ذ يِللة لِمن فعل يِب ولفخر‬
ِ ‫أنا أرض ا‬
ِ ‫ الشفاء يِف ترب يِت و م يِائ ولفخر بل خ‬.‫هلل المقدس ِة المبارك ِة‬
ِ ِ‫ن بل شكرا  لهل‬
ِ‫ع من دو ي‬

I am the sacred and blessed land of Allah. Cure has been placed in my dust and water, and I am not arrogant.
Rather, I am humble and humiliated before He who has blessed me. I do not boast to those who are lower than
me in rank. On the contrary, I am thankful to Allah.
So, Allah honored it, increased His blessings upon it for its humility, and rewarded it with by burying in its land
Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) and his companions. Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) added:

َ َ ْ َ َ ُ ّٰ‫َ ْ َ َ َ َ للِهَّ َ َ َ ُ ه‬
َ َّ‫ك ر‬
ُ ّٰ‫ب َو َض َع ُه ه‬
ٰ َ‫الل َت َع ي‬
‫ال‬
‫من تواضع ِ رفعه الل و من ت‬

"Allah elevates those who humble themselves before Him and He degrades those who are arrogant.”

Kāmil al-Ziyārah, P. 821, Ibn Qulawayh

Kaʿbah & Karbalāʾ 267

Bayn ul-Ḥaramayn & Ṣafā and Marwah

There is a distance of 377 meters
(412 yards) between the mountains of Ṣafā and Marwah, where
pilgrims perform their saʿī.

This is the same distance that
is between the shrines of Imām
Ḥusayn (ʿa) and Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa).

Map of the Holy Shrine of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa) 271

Etiquette of Ziyārah of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa)
The status of infallibility is manifested completely within the 14
Maʿṣūmīn, while others have been able to reach it to some extent,
such as Sayyidah Zaynab, ʿAlī Akbar, Sayyidah Maʿsūmah, and
Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa).
Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa) is a personality that has reached a very high
level of ʿiṣmah (infallibility). In fact, he has reached such a high
level that some of the aḥkām, etiquettes, and mustaḥabāt of his
ziyārah and ḥaram are similar to those of the 14 Maʿṣūmīn.
 Just as we perform ziyārah of the Maʿṣūmīn, for the ziyarah of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās it is also
recommended to stand with your back towards the qiblah and your front towards the
ḍarīḥ.
 Ṣalāt ul-Ziyārah (a two-rakaʿāt prayer after reciting ziyārah), which is recommended for
the 14 Maʿṣūmīn, is also recommended for Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās.
 It is highly recommended for those who are in the state of janābah or ḥaydh not to
enter the shrine of ḤaḍratʿAbbās (ʿa), just as with the 14 Maʿsūmīn.

In Rememberance of Umm al-Banīn
Even though Umm al-Banīn was not in Karbalāʾ, many pilgrims do the following when they
want to exit the hall after performing the ziyārah of ʿAbbās (ʿa). They stand by the western
door next to the minaret, take the name of Umm al-Banīn, and take blessings from that
doorway, as if to say, “O Umm al-Banīn, we will never forget your sacrifices! All praise be
upon you and your brave children!” This is why this door has been named the Door of Umm
al-Banīn.

Ziyārah of Umm al-Banīn 273

Ziyārah of Umm al-Banīn
Umm al-Banīn, whose given name was Fāṭimah, was a brave, courageous, noble, and sincere
woman who became the wife of Amīr al-Muʾminīn after the martyrdom of Sayyidah Fāṭimah azZahrāʾ (ʿa). Together, they had four children: ʿAbbās, ʿAbdullāh, Jaʿfar, and ʿUthmān. It is because
of these four sons that she was given the title Umm al-Banīn, which means "Mother of sons."
These sons became the four men who followed in Imām Ḥusayn's footsteps and defended him
valiantly in Karbalāʾ. Although Umm al-Banīn was not present in Karbalāʾ to witness the events
of that sorrowful day, she mourned for the martyrs and her four sons, and even wrote poems in
their rememberance.
One who wishes to perform the ziyārah of Umm al-Banīn can recite the following:

The Maqām of al-ʿAbbās's Right Hand 285

The Maqām of al-ʿAbbās's Right Hand
Ibn Shahr Āshūb said: ʿAbbās (ʿa) was the Sāqī (water
bearer), Qamar Banī Hāshim (Moon of Banī Hāshim),
and the flagbearer of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa). He came to
get water, and they attacked him and he confronted
them saying:

َ
َ ‫الأرهب املوت إذ املوت‬
َّ‫رىق حتى‬
‫أوارى يف املصايلت لقا‬
ّ‫ي‬
ّ
ّ
ّ َ‫نفيس نلفس املصطىف‬
‫الطهر وقا إن أنا العباس أغدوا بالسقا‬
ّ ‫و الأخاف‬
‫الرش يوم امللتيق‬

I never fear death when it comes around.
May my life be sacrificed for the life of the pure Muṣtafā!
I am al-ʿAbbās, the Saqqā, who has no fear of the evil
and I will make the enemy scatter.
Zayd ibn Warqā was hiding behind a palm tree.
Along with Hakīm ibn Tufayl, he struck the right hand
of ʿAbbās (ʿa). So,ʿAbbās switched the sword and
waterskin to his left and chanted:

ُ ّ‫ي‬
ً
‫إن أحايم أبدا عن ديين واهلل إن قطعتم يميين‬
ّ ‫يب‬
ّ ‫جنل‬
ّ ‫انل‬
‫الطاهر األمني و عن إمام صادق ايلقني‬

By Allah! If you cut off my right hand,
I shall not cease defending my religion!
An Imām true to his conviction do I defend,
A son of the pure and trustworthy Prophet, whom
Allah did send.

Place of the right hand of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās

Towards the northeast and southeast of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās’s
courtyard, there are two places where the blessed
hands of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa) were severed.

286 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

The Maqām of al-ʿAbbās's Left Hand
Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās (ʿa) continued to fight. Meanwhile,
Hakīm ibn Tufayl, who was hiding behind another
palm tree, came out and struck the left arm of Ḥaḍrat
ʿAbbās (ʿa), who then said:

ّ
‫يَا نفس الختيش من الكفار‬‭‬
ّ ‫و أبرشي برمحة‬
‫اجلبار‬
ّ ‫يب‬
ّ ‫مع‬
ّ ‫انل‬
‫الس ّيد املختار‬
ّ
َ
ّ
ّ
‫يا رب حر انلار‬‭‬‫قدقطعوا ببغيهم يساري فأصلهم‬

O Self, do not fear the infidels!
And be glad [to receive] the Mercy of the Almighty,
with the Prophet, the master of chosen ones,
along with the masters and pure ones.
They have cut off my left [arm] with their tyranny,
so burn them, O Lord, with the heat of the fire!
Alas, ʿAbbās (ʿa) was struck with a metal club and fell
to the sands of Karbalāʾ. Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) rushed
towards his brother and found him lying on the ground
by the Euphrates River. He cried
out:
ّ
ّ
ّ

ّ َ‫ي‬‭‬
ّ ‫ارش قوم بفعلكم و خالفتم قول انل‬
‫يب حممد تعديتم‬
ّ
ّ ‫الرسل‬
ّ ‫أما اكن خري‬
ّ ‫وصاكم بنا أما حنن من نسل‬
ّ ‫انل‬
‫يب املسدد‬
ّ ‫أم دونكم أما اكن من خري‬
ّ ‫أما اكنت‬
َ ‫الزهراء‬
‫الربية أمحد‬

ّ ‫لعنتم و أُخزيتم بما قدجنيتم فسوف تالقوا‬
‫حر نار توقد‬
O the worst of people! You have opposed the orders of the Prophet (ṣ) with this tyrannical and
oppressive act. Didn’t the best of messengers advise you to love and obey us? Are we not from
the lineage of the chosen Prophet (ṣ) that have been chosen? Is Fāṭimah az-Zahrāʾ (ʿa) your
mother or ours? Was she not the best of creations from Aḥmad? You have been cursed and
disgraced due to this act you have committed. You will soon taste the heat of the fire and its
scorching flames.

Maqām of Ṣāḥib az-Zamān (ʿaj) 287

Maqām of Ṣāḥib az-Zamān (ʿaj)
The Maqām of Ṣāḥib az-Zamān (ʿaj) is located on the path to Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq’s (ʿa) maqām and
contains a high level of spirit and hope for those hearts seeking to reconnect with the Imām of
the time, and who are awaiting his blissful return. It is widely believed that Imām Mahdī (ʿaj) was
present here, and thus, this place holds a certain blessing. It is recommended to come here and
pray for his reappearance. May Allah the Almighty illuminate our eyes through his blissful return.
There is a river next to the maqām that is connected to the Euphrates.

az-Zamān (ʿaj)

The Euphrates River

289

The Euphrates River

Qi
bla
hS
tre
et

The supreme event of Karbalāʾ occurred near the Euphrates River (Furāt). Today, this river is 20
km east of Karbalāʾ. According to narrations, the water of the Furāt has many virtues and blessings,
some of which are mentioned below:
 Drinking from it is mustaḥab.
 It is mustaḥab to give newborns a taste of the water of furāt and turbah of Abā ʿAbdillah.
 Whoever performs ghusl with water from the Euphrates River.
 Reminder: You don’t have to go into the actual river to get the blessings of the Euphrates. The
tap water in Karbalāʾ is from the Euphrates, so inshā’Allah using the tap water has the same
bounties and blessings.
 The ʿAlqamah River is a branch of the Euphrates that flows from Karbalāʾ to Kūfah. It used to be
on the eastern part of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās's ḥaram, but has now dried up, which is why that street is
known as ʿAlqamah Street.

290 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Al-Mukhayyam: The Campsite

291

Al-Mukhayyam: The Campsite
When Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) reached
Karbalāʾ on 2nd Muḥarram, 61
AH, he ordered his men to set
up their tents in a place known
as al-Mukhayyam, Khaymagah,
or the campsite.
This location was away from the
actual battlefield, and the Imām
(ʿa) had dug a trench behind it,
blocking the enemies from attacking the tents.
The Imām’s (ʿa) family, along with Sayyidah Zaynab, and all the Banī
Hāshim stayed within these tents.1
The location of every single tent was very carefully thought out. The
Imām’s (ʿa) tent, along with Sayyidah Zaynab’s, was in the center
while the tents of Banī Hāshim were surrounding them.2
Other features of those tents include:
 Some of the tents were used as supplies tents to gather food
and water.
 Despite the lack of people, everything was very well-organized.
 There was a tent designated exclusively for the bodies of the
martyrs.
 After the shahādah of Imām Ḥusayn, the enemies attacked the
tents, looted everything they could find, and set fire them.

Some of the Tents of Imām
Ḥusayn (ʿa)
• Commander's tent
• Medical tent
• Tent of water provision
• Tent of shuhadāʾ
• Storage tent
• Strategizing tent
• Tent of Imām as-Sajjād (ʿa)
• Tent of companions
• Tent of Banī Hāshim
• Family tent
• Tent of Sayyidah Zaynab (ʿa)

292 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Today, al-Mukhayyam has a symbolic structure resembling
the exact position of the tents back then. One can see the tents
of the Imām and his family, such as the tent of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
and his miḥrāb, the tent of Imām as-Sajjād (ʿa), and the tent of
Qāsim.

1. Ḥayyāt al-Imām Ḥusayn, Vol. 3, P. 93
2. The Life of Sayyid ash-Shuhadāʾ P. 329, Ḥusayn ʿImādzadeh

Tal az-Zaynabiyyah

Tal az-Zaynabiyyah

Tal az-Zaynabiyyah (The Hill of Zaynab) is located southwest of the holy
shrine. It has been written in the book of Tārikh wa Jughrāfiyā Karbalāʾ:
“On the day of ʿĀshūrāʾ, Sayyidah Zaynab used to stand on this hill and
oversee the maqtal (battlefield) and would follow every step of her brother, Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa), with her eyes. Many times, she went up the hill in a
state of fear, and it has been reported that she mourned and expressed
her grief for many incidents from atop that hill.”
How difficult it must have been to witness all of those heinous acts that
the son of Amīr al-Muʾminīn (ʿa) and Sayyidah Fāṭimah az-Zahrāʾ (ʿa)
was suffering from! Indeed, she was given divine tolerance when Imām
Ḥusayn put his hand over her chest and recited duʿā in order to help her
bear witnessing such scenes.

An old picture of Tal az-Zaynabiyyah before reconstruction

Even with all of her greatness,
unfortunately, no narrated
ziyārah of Sayyidah Zaynab
has reached us today. Ziyārāt
that exist today are pieces
put together from history. If
a pilgrim wants to recite a
ziyārah at this location for
her, it is recommended they
recite the ziyārah of Sayyidah
Maʿṣūmah found in Mafātih alJinān.

Maqām Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) 295

Maqām Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa)
Maqām of Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa) is
located on the northern side of Imām
Ḥusayn’s (ʿa) shrine, as you pass the
Nahr al-Ḥusayniyyah and walk through
gardens known as Jaʿfariyyāt. Thirty
meters in, you will reach this place
where it is said Imām Ja’far aṣ-Ṣādiq
(ʿa) used to reside. He would perform
ghusl with the water of the Euprhates
and then go towards the ḥaram to
perform ziyārah.
The maqām used to be a hexagon shaped building with a green
dome on top. However, after the Intifāḍah Shaʿbāniyya of 1991,
Saddam began destroying religious monuments and masājid.
During this time, this maqām was also leveled to the ground.
One of the neighboring landlords rebuilt it in 1994, but it was
left without a caretaker due to security precautions, as it was
too close to a military base. This strategic placement allowed
Saddam's forces to prevent any locals or pilgrims from visiting
this place.
Today, this maqām has expanded by 600 m2. There is a beautiful
gate at the entrance, as well as a large courtyard where pilgrims
rest.

296 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Karbalāʾ

Al-Ḥurr
Al-Ḥurr, the son of Yazīd ibn al-Nājīya al-Tamīmī al-Rīyāḥī was from
the tribe of Banī Tamīm. He was well-known in his tribe and in Kūfah. In
the year 60 AH, he was appointed by ʿUbaydullāh ibn Ziyād as the commander of 30,000 militants from the Banī Tamīm and Ḥamdan tribes.
After ʿUmar ibn Saʿad, he was the most important figure of the Kufan
Army in the battle of Karbalāʾ and was tasked with the mission to block
the path of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa).
As he and his men reached the Imām’s (ʿa) caravan, the Imām (ʿa) ordered his men to provide water for Ḥurr and his troops, and the Imām
(ʿa) himself even brought some water to Ḥurr. This compassion shown
by the Imām (ʿa) awakened Ḥurr’s soul, leading to a shift in his behavior
to such an extent that on the 8th of Muḥarram, ibn Saʿad repositioned
him further from the Imām.
But the touch of an Infallible (ʿa) did not stop there. Once the Truth sheds some light on the
heart of a believer who has the capacity to bear the Truth, it will work its charm. So, on the day
of ʿĀshūrāʾ, he finally made up his mind and used the excuse of watering his horse to break
away from ibn Saʿad’s army and joined Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa). The minute he was pardoned from
the Imām (ʿa), he asked for permission to be the first one in the battlefield. He tried to talk with
the people of Kūfah and warn them about conducting the biggest mistake of their lives. A group
of the enemies were moved by his speech and wanted to end the war, but the rest of the army
began launching arrows at him. After a great battle, Ayyūb ibn Musarraḥ martyred al-Ḥurr.
Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) rushed towards him As Ḥurr was taking his last few breaths, the Imām placed
Ḥurr’s head on his lap, and said:
ُ َ ْ َ َ ْ ُّ
ُ َ ْ َ َ ُّ ُ َ َّ َ َ َ ُ َ ْ َ
‫األخ َرة‬
ِ ‫أنت ح ٌّر كما سمتك أمك َو أنت ح ٌّر يِف ادلنيا َو أنت ح ٌّر يِف‬
You are Ḥurr (free) just as your mother named you— free in this world and free in the hereafter.

The Imām then closed Ḥurr’s eyes and tied the wound on his head with a piece of cloth.

Ziyārah of Al-Ḥurr 297

Location of Al-Ḥurr's Shrine
Ḥurr's tomb is located in a place called al-Ḥur, approximately four miles northwest of Imām Ḥusayn’s
shrine. He is this far away because when his tribesmen heard that the army of ʿUmar ibn Saʿad wanted
to trample the bodies, they took his body and buried
him in a place called Nawāmis.
His shrine was first built upon the order of Shāh
Ismāʿīl Ṣafawī. He ordered his grave to be opened,
and they found his body untouched, just as if he had
been killed yesterday, and the handkerchief which Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
had tied around his head was there, as well. Shāh Ismāʿīl opened
the handkerchief, and fresh blood started flowing down and would not
stop with any other handkerchief. So, they had to return the very same
handkerchief to his head. It was right then that Shāh Ismāʿīl Ṣafawī
ordered for his shrine to be built.
Imām az-Zamān (ʿaj) has sent his salāms upon Ḥurr twice: once
in ziyārah ar-Rajabiyyah and the other in ziyārah an-Nāḥiyyah alMuqaddasah.

Awlad Muslim: The Sons of Muslim ibn ʿAqīl
The shrine of the sons of Muslim ibn ʿAqīl is
located in the city of Musayyib, which is 35
km outside of Karbalāʾ towards Baghdad.
After killing Muslim ibn ʿAqīl, Ibn Ziyād imprisoned his two sons, Muḥammad and
Ibrāhīm. However, the guard realized these
were descendants of ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib (ʿa),
and he allowed them to escape. The two
young boys wandered around the city of
Kūfah and finally took refuge at night time in
the home of a pious woman. However, this
woman’s husband, Ḥārith, had been looking
for these two children, as there was a lofty
bounty offered for their capture.
When her husband came home, he quickly
realized that the two boys were in his own
house. In the morning, he beheaded both
boys and threw their bodies into the Euphrates River. He then took their heads to Ibn
Ziyād to collect his reward. However, despite
being such a a cold-hearted man, when Ibn
Ziyād saw the two small heads, he could not
bare seeing this. Therefore, he commanded
that Ḥārith himself be beheaded in the same
place where he beheaded the two boys.

The Euphrates River brought their bodies
to this location, where they were discovered by local villagers. After they realized
who these bodies belong to, they buried
them. Their graves were later turned into
a shrine; many zuwwār make it a point to
visit the ḥaram of these two boys and offer
their respects and salāms.

Awlad Muslim: The Sons of Muslim ibn ʿAqīl 301

The Adab (Etiquette) of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās towards his Imām (ʿa)

This is an aerial picture of Ḥaḍrat ʿAbbās’s (ʿa) ḥaram in
relation to Imām Ḥusayn’s (ʿa) ḥaram. You can see that Ḥaḍrat
ʿAbbās’s (ʿa) grave is positioned behind Imām Ḥusayn’s (ʿa)
grave, just as you would see an Imām stands in front of the
followers in congregational prayers.

Rewards of Performing Ziyārah on Foot
Performing ziyārah of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) on foot has
many rewards, which is why our scholars place great
emphasis on it.

Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa): When one leaves his/her
house to perform the ziyārah of Imām Ḥusayn
(ʿa) by foot, one good act will be written and one
sin will be removed for every step he/she takes.1

aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa), narrates: I went to visit Imām

talking to Allah after completing his ṣalāh, and he was
reciting the following prayer for the pilgrims of Imām

1. Biḥār al-Anwār Vol. 89 P. 82

Some Great Scholars Walking to Karbalāʾ

Late Āyatullāh
Khoei in his youth

Late Āyatullāh
Mirza Jawad
Tabrizi

Āyatullāh Sayyid
Muhammad Saeed
Hakim

The tradition of performing ziyārah on foot has been practiced
since the time of the Maʿṣūmīn (ʿa). The reward for this action
cannot even be measured. Faḍil Darbandī writes:

The act of walking to perform ziyārah is either due to a lack of
money, which shows the pilgrim’s level of enthusiasm and passion, or it is due to the pilgrim viewing him or herself humbly in
comparison to the role model of martyrdom. In either of these situations, the pilgrim will be able to tolerate every little pain and hardship during such a journey, and both cases are extremely precious.3

It has been the tradition in Iraq for individuals, groups, and caravans to walk from various cities, such as
Najaf, Baṣrah, and Baghdad, towards Karbalāʾ. The walk is done more frequently during peak times, such
as Arbaʿīn, the week of ʿĀshūrāʾ, 15th Shaʿbān, and 1st Rajab.
Many of our great scholars have participated in this tradition as well. This walk would provide many new
tablīgh opportunities, while people were mourning and reciting poems on the path.

During the regime of Saddam, such walks themselves were viewed as a movement against the regime, especially while walking on the unofficial path through the palm tree lands by the Euphrates River. In the year
1397 AH, while this walk was taking place, an intense battle erupted between the army and the pilgrims,
leaving many pilgrims wounded or killed.
3. Isrār ash-Shahādah,Vol. 89 P. 631, Fāḍil Darbandī

Rewards of Performing Ziyārah on Foot 305

Shahīd Sayyid
Muḥammad Taqī Jalālī

Shahīd Āyatullāh Sayyid
Muṣṭafā Khomeini

Shahīd Sayyid ʿAbd aṣ-Ṣāḥib and Shahīd Oldest picture of the walk to Karbalāʾ

(1916)

After the downfall of Saddam, the Shīʿah had a fervent desire to establish the tradition of walking from Najaf to Karbalāʿ, so they started
building mawākib (resting areas) on the path from Najaf to Karbalāʾ.

Ziyārat Arbaʿīn
Shaykh Ṭūsī in Tahzīb and Miṣbāḥ narrates this ḥadīth of Imām Ḥasan al-ʿAskarī (ʿa):
The signs of a muʾmin (believer) are five:
 Reciting 51 rakaʿāt everyday, out of which 17 rakaʿāt are mandatory and 34 are nāfilah
(recommended)
 Reciting Ziyārat al-Arbaʿīn
 Wearing a ring on the right hand
 Placing one’s forehead on the soil (during sajdah)
َّ ‫الر مْحٰن‬
َّ ‫ ِمْسِب اهلل‬out loud
 Reciting ‫الر ِحيْ ْم‬
ِ
ِ
On the 20th of Ṣafar, the caravan of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) arrived in Karbala, returning from Damascus. On this day, Jābir ibn ʿAbd Allah al-Anṣārī performed the first visit to the grave of Imām
Ḥusayn. Therefore, it is recommended to visit the holy shrine of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) on this day.
The following ziyārah is narrated by Ṣafwān Jamāl from Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa):
On the day of Arbaʿīn, recite the following a few hours before ẓuhr:
Peace be upon the close guardian of Allah
and His most beloved.
Peace be upon the friend of Allah and His
elite.
Peace be upon the choice of Allah and son
of His choice.
Peace be upon al-Ḥusayn, the wronged and
martyred.
Peace be upon the prisoners of agony
and victims who were killed as their family
members watched tearfully.

ْ َ ُ َ ُ َ َ ُ ْ َ َّ َ َ ْ َ

‫هلل‬
‫حه ِمائة أل ِف نَبيِ ٍ و أربعة و ِع‬
ِ‫من أحب أن يصاف‬
ِ ‫شون ألف نَبيِ ٍ ّ فلير ق أ يِب عب ِد ا‬

‫يستأ ِذنون اهلل يِف ِزيارتِ ِه فيؤذن لهم ِمنهم خسة أولو العزمِ ِمن‬

‫ن أولو ال َع ْزمِ ؟‬
َْ‫رَ ْ أ‬

ََ‫ بُ ِعثُوا إلى‬:‫قَ َال‬
‫ش ِق ال ْر ِض َو غ ْربِ َها ِج ِن َها َو ِإن ِس َها‬
ِ

It has been narrated from Imām aṣ-Ṣādiq and Imām ʿAlī ibn al-Ḥusayn (ʿa)
that:
"One who wishes to greet all 124,000 Prophets should visit the grave of
Imām Ḥusayn ibn ʿAlī (ʿa) on the 15th of Shaʿbān because the souls of
the Prophets have taken permission from Allah to perform the ziyārah of
the Imām (ʿa) on that night, and the Almighty granted their request. Five
of them are the Ūlūl ʿAẓm Prophets."
It was asked, “Who are they?”
The Imām replied, “Prophets Nūḥ, Ibrāhīm, Mūsā, ʿĪsā, and Muḥammad
(ṣ)”
We asked, “What is the meaning of Ūlūl ʿAzm?”
The Imām (ʿa) replied, “Those prophets who have been raised to guide
everyone in the west and the east from among the jinns and human
beings.”
Kāmil az-Ziyārah, P. 594

Imām Ḥusayn’s (ʿa) Ziyārah on the 15th of Shaʿbān 313

Imām Jaʿfar aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa):

On the 15th of Shaʿbān, a caller announces
from the highest horizon, “O visitors of Ḥusayn
(ʿa), return [to your homes] forgiven; your rewards will be given by Allah, your Lord, and by
Muḥammad (ṣ), your Prophet.”
Kāmil az-Ziyārah, P. 593

Imām Jaʿfar aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa):

Whoever visits the grave of Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
on the eve of the 15th of Shaʿbān, Allah will
forgive his past and future sins; and whoever
visits him on the day of ʿArafah, Allah will write
for him the rewards of 1,000 accepted Ḥajj
and 1,000 accepted ʿUmrah; and whoever
visits him on the day of ʿĀshūrāʾ, it will be like
he is visiting Allah at His throne.
Kāmil az-Ziyārah, P. 599

Imām Jaʿfar aṣ-Ṣādiq (ʿa):

Allah will forgive the past and future sins of anyone who visits Ḥusayn ibn ʿAlī (ʿa) on one of
three eves. I humbly asked, “May I be sacrificed
for you. What are those three eves?” The Imām
(ʿa) replied, “The eve of ʿĪd al-Fiṭr, the eve of ʿĪd
al-Aḍḥā, and the eve of 15th Shaʿbān.”
Kāmil az-Ziyārah, P. 596

Imām Muḥammad al-Bāqir (ʿa):

The sins of one who visits Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa) on
the 15th of Shaʿbān will be forgiven, and no sins
will be recorded for him during the remainder
of that year, and if he visits Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa)
again the following 15th Shaʿbān, Allah will
forgive all his sins.
Kāmil az-Ziyārah, P. 596

Virtues of Ziyārah of Imām
Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa) and Imām
Muḥammad al-Jawād (ʿa)

There are many narrations regarding the virtues
and bounties of performing their ziyārah:
• Performing the ziyārah of Imām Mūsā ibn Jaʿfar
(ʿa) is like performing the ziyārah of the Noble
Prophet (ṣ), and visiting him is like visiting the
Noble Prophet (ṣ), Amīr al-Mu’minīn (ʿa), and
Imām Ḥusayn (ʿa).1

seeking refuge in the holy shrine of Mūsā ibn
Jaʿfar (peace be upon him) and seeking his
intercession.3
• Imām ar-Riḍā (ʿa): Allah saved the city of
Baghdād by placing the graves of Imām alKāẓim and Imām al-Jawād in it.

• Whoever performs the ziyārah of Imām Mūsā ibn
Jaʿfar (ʿa) [with maʿrifah (deep understanding)] is
among the people of Heaven.2
• Ibn Shahr Āshūb narrates from Khaṭīb alBaghdādī, the author of Tārīkh Baghdād, from
ʿAlī ibn Khilāl: Every problem that I faced was
resolved and made easy by the Almighty through

2. Ibid, P. 545
3. Ibn Shahr Āshūb, Manāqib Āl Abī Ṭālib, Vol. 4, P. 305

Virtues of Ziyārah of Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa) and Imām Muḥammad al-Jawād (ʿa) 317

Jawād means to give to one who does or doesn't deserve;
grant me a big heart, and in your way the chance to serve!

320 An Illustrated Ziyārah Guide to Irāq: Kaẓimayn

History of Kāẓimayn


145 AH: This area used to be a garden called Shuniziyah next to Baghdād. Al-Manṣūr selected this
garden to be the Graveyard of the Quraysh.



179 AH: Upon the order of Hārūn al-ʿAbbāsī, Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa) was transported from Madīnah and
imprisoned in Baghdād.



183 AH: Sindī ibn Shāhik poisoned and martyred Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa) upon the order of Hārūn al-



183 AH: The holy body of Imām al-Kāẓim (ʿa) was buried in a land he had purchased earlier.



220 AH: Imām al-Jawād (ʿa) was poisoned and martyred upon the order of al-Muʾtaṣim and was buried
alongside his grandfather. A structure was built over their holy and blessed graves, and that area was
named Kāẓimiyyah.



336 AH: Upon the order of Muʿizz ad-Dawlah (Buyid Dynasty), two new gravestones were built, along
with two wooden ḍariḥs.



369 AH: ʿAḍud ad-Dawlah extended the shrine and built a wall around the city, distinguishing Kāẓimayn.

ʿAbbāsī.

History of Kāẓimayn 321



490 AH: The walls of the shrine were tiled by Majd al-Mulk. He also built a great masjid with two beautiful
minarets on the northern side of the shrine.



569 AH: Flooding of the Tigris River caused some damages to the holy courtyard, as well as the shrine.



575 AH: Al-Nāṣir li-Dīn Allah, with the help of his Shīʿah vizier, constructed rooms around the shrine and
setup the Dār aḍ-Ḍiyāfah (guesthouse).



608 AH: The ʿAbbāsid khalīfah converted the rooms around the shrine into an Islamic seminary.



656 AH: The Mongol ruler Hūlāgū Khān attacked Baghdād, damaging Kāẓimayn as well.



658 AH: ʿAṭā Malik al-Juwaynī, the minister of Hūlāgū Khān, paid for the damages caused to Kāẓimayn
and began rebuilding it.



776 AH: Flooding of the Tigris River caused damage to the shrine. Sulṭān ʿUways Jalāyirī repaired these
damages.



926 AH: Shāh Ismāʿīl Ṣafawī constructed a magnificent building, a masjid, and two mosaic domes on the
northern side of the shrine.



1045 AH: Shāh Ṣafawī built four minarets on the corners of the courtyard, which still exist today.



1211 AH: Āghā Muḥammad Khān Qājār gilded the two domes and covered the ground and courtyard of
the shrine in marble.



1229 AH: Fatḥ-ʿAlī Shāh Qājār adorned the interior of the shrine with intricate mirror work and gilded the
minarets.



1255 AH: Muʿtamid ad-Dawlah gilded the porches around the shrine.



1282 AH: Shaykh al-‘Irāqayn, the representative of Nāsīr ad-Din Shāh Qājār, adorned the porches with
mirror work and gilded them; he also adorned the courtyard with mosaic tiles. Farhād Mīrzā, son of ʿAbbās
Mīrzā, played an instrumental role in rebuilding the shrine and was buried inside the shrine.

Entering the Holy Shrine
It has been narrated from Sayyid ibn Ṭāwūs that one should perform ghusl and then
humbly walk towards the holy shrine. When you reach the gate to the ḥaram, stop and
recite:
Allah is the Greatest! Allah is the
Greatest! There is no god except Allah,
and Allah is the Greatest. All praise is
for Allah for guiding me to His religion
and  making me successful in answering
the call to (performing my duties in) His
path.
O Allah! You are the Most Honorable
one who anyone intends to visit. Surely,
I have come to You, seeking nearness
to You through the grandson of Your
Prophet, may Your blessings be upon
him, his pure forefathers, and his
immaculate progeny.
O Allah, send Your blessings and mercy
on Muḥammad and his holy household
and do not deny my request or cut off
my hope. And make me honorable in
this life and in the hereafter and amongst
those who are close to You.

Entering the Holy Shrine 325

When entering, enter with your right foot and recite:
With the name of Allah (I begin), in Allah (I trust),
in the path of Allah (I tread), and upon the creed
of Rasūl Allah (I proceed), may Allah bless him
and his household.
O Allah, please forgive me, my parents and all
the believing men and women.

Ziyārah of Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa) 327

Ziyārah of Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa)
Then, enter, say Allahu Akbar 4 times, face the grave with your back to the qiblah and
recite:
Peace be upon you, O guardian of Allah
and son of His guardian. Peace be upon
you, O proof of Allah and son of His
proof.
Peace be upon you, O Allah’s chosen
one and son of His chosen one. Peace
be upon you, O Allah’s trustee and son
of His trustee.
Peace be upon you, O Allah’s light in the
darkness of the earth. Peace be upon
you, O leader of true guidance. Peace
be upon you, O the banner of religion
and piety.
Peace be upon you, O the treasure of
the Prophets' knowledge. Peace be
upon you, O treasure of the Messengers'
knowledge.
Peace be upon you, O deputy of the
preceding successors (of the Prophets).
Peace be upon you, O source of the
clear revelation.

I also bear witness that you passed away
upon the same principles on which your
immaculate fathers and pure forefathers,
the successors, guides, leaders, and rightly
guided ones, passed away.
You never preferred blindness over true
guidance and never slanted from the truth
to falsehood. I also bear witness that you
acted sincerely for Allah, His Messenger,
and the Commander of the Faithful.

your loyalists, declaring animosity towards
your enemies,

Then, kiss the ḍarīḥ, place both sides of your face on it, and ask for your needs. Then,
come back near the holy head and say:
Peace be upon you, O my master, Mūsā,
son of Jaʿfar. May Allah’s mercy and
blessings be upon you.
I bear witness that you are surely the guiding
leader and the guardian who nurtures (us)
to true guidance.
You are surely the core of the Revelation,
the master of true interpretation,   the
bearer of the Torah and the Bible, and the
knowledgeable, just, and truthful one who
puts his knowledge into practice.
O my master, I disassociate from your enemies
in the presence of Allah, and I seek nearness
to Allah through my loyalty towards you.
So, may Allah bless you, your fathers,
your forefathers, your descendants, your
followers, and your lovers. May Allah’s
mercy and blessings be upon them.

Ṣalawāt of Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa) 333

Ṣalawāt of Imām Mūsā al-Kāẓim (ʿa)
Sayyid ibn Ṭāwūs narrates the following Ṣalawāt of Imām Mūsā bin Jaʿfar (ʿa), which
divulges the virtues and tragedies of the Imām (ʿa):
O Allah, send blessings upon Muḥammad
and his household and send blessings
upon Mūsā, son of Jaʿfar, the successor of
the righteous ones,
the leader of the excellent ones, the
treasure of illumination, and the inheritor of
tranquility, dignity, wisdom, and traditions.
He used to stay awake during the night until
early dawn, continuously imploring (Allah)
for forgiveness.
He was inseparably attached to lengthy
prostrations, heavy tears, long confidential
talks, and unending implorations.
He was the center of understanding,
justice, goodness, virtue, munificence, and
generosity.

He is the one who joined his grandfather
(the Prophet), the chosen one, his father
(Imām ʿAlī), the content one, and his
mother (Sayyidah Fāṭimah), the leader
of the women, with usurped inheritance,
robbed loyalty, overpowered state,
unavenged blood, and having drunk
poison.
O Allah, just as he patiently endured
difficult ordeals, swallowed his grief and
tragedies,
submitted to Your pleasure, obeyed You
sincerely, adopted (internal) humility
towards You,

and adopted (external) humility towards
You, stood against innovation (bidʿat) and
its bearers,
and was not influenced by those who
taunted him, in regards to following
Your orders and refraining from Your
prohibitions;
thus, bless him with ever-increasing, lofty,
and purified blessings that will allow all
Your creations to receive his intercession.

And convey to him our greetings and
peace, and grant us from Your special
blessings, favors, bounties, forgiveness,
and pleasure on account of our loyalty to
him.
Surely, You are the Owner of prevalent
favors and supreme exoneration. By Your
Mercy, O the Most Merciful!

Ziyārah of Imām Muḥammad al-Jawād (ʿa)
Then, turn towards the grave of Imām Muḥammad bin ʿAlī al-Jawād, which is next to the grave
of his grandfather, and recite the following:

Common Ziyārah of Imām al-Kāzim (ʿa) and Imām al-Jawād (ʿa)
The two great scholars Shaykh al-Mufīd and Muḥammad bin Mashhadī have said that the
moment you reach the pure ḍarīḥ, stand there and recite the following:

Peace be upon you O representatives
of Allah! Peace be upon you O proofs of
Allah! Peace be upon you O the lights of
Allah in the darkness of the earth.
I bear witness that you both faithfully
conveyed that which Allah ordered you
to convey, and that you safeguarded
that which He entrusted you with. I bear
witness that you prescribed that which
Allah has made lawful and prohibited that
which Allah has made unlawful,
and that you established the boundaries
set by Allah, recited the book of Allah,
and endured harm for the sake of Allah
patiently while directing affairs in the light
of the divine rules until death came to you.

Farewell Ziyārah of Imām Mūsā al-Kaẓim (ʿa) 343

Farewell Ziyārah of Imām Mūsā al-Kaẓim (ʿa)
Peace be upon you, O my master, O Abā alḤasan, and the mercy and blessings of Allah.
I entrust you in Allah's care and send my
salutations upon you. I have believed in
Allah, the Messenger, and that which he
has brought and guided us to.
O Allah, write our names amongst the
martyrs.
